The conference brought together key units of the Municipal Forest Fire Prevention Office, including the Municipal Planning and Resources Department, Public Security Department, Industry and Information Technology Department, Civil Affairs Department, Culture and Tourism Department, Agriculture Committee, and Fire Department, along with the Forest Fire Prevention Offices of all agricultural districts and relevant units, to analyze the forest fire prevention work situation during the critical period and arrange related work.

  Instance 4: 9 -- Ministry of Emergency Management of the People's Republic of China issued the following news release:During key periods, the Tianjin Forest Fire Prevention and Suppression Command Office has firmly established bottom-line thinking and extreme thinking, kept a close eye on important time nodes, key areas and important targets, maintained a high level of vigilance, and taken effective measures to ensure that the forest fire prevention situation remains stable.Comprehensively coordinate and coordinate forest fire prevention work. In mid-August, the Municipal Forest Fire Prevention Office held a video conference on forest fire prevention and control during the critical period. The conference brought together key units of the Municipal Forest Fire Prevention Office, including the Municipal Planning and Resources Department, Public Security Department, Industry and Information Technology Department, Civil Affairs Department, Culture and Tourism Department, Agriculture Committee, and Fire Department, along with the Forest Fire Prevention Offices of all agricultural districts and relevant units, to analyze the forest fire prevention work situation during the critical period and arrange related work. At the meeting, the Municipal Planning and Resources Department, Public Security Department, and Industry and Information Technology Department put forward specific requirements for relevant industry sectors during the critical period. The Municipal Forest Fire Prevention Office deployed forest fire prevention and control work for the city during the critical period, focusing on fire prevention publicity, hazard investigation and remediation, fire risk monitoring, patrols, and pre-deployment of teams and equipment.

  Instance 1: urn:contentItem:6H3J-8083-S86J-437W-00000-00Researchers at Universiti Kebangsaan Malaysia Report Research in Engineering (Satellite-Based Forest Fire Mapping Using Group and Shuffle Network Embeddings)2025-10-31T00:00:00Z2025-11-03T19:29:27ZLexisNexisENGINEERINGResearchers at Universiti Kebangsaan Malaysia Report Research in Engineering (Satellite-Based Forest Fire Mapping Using Group and Shuffle Network Embeddings)2025 OCT 31 (NewsRx) -- By a News Reporter-Staff News Editor at Engineering Daily News -- Investigators publish new report on engineering. According to news originating from Bangi, Malaysia, by NewsRx editors, the research stated, "Forest fire mapping plays a vital role in environmental monitoring and disaster response."  Financial supporters for this research include Ministry of Higher Education, Malaysia, Through The Fundamental Research Grant Scheme; Universiti Kebangsaan Malaysia Through Dana Padanan Kolaborasi-geran Pembiayaan Sepadan. The news journalists obtained a quote from the research from Universiti Kebangsaan Malaysia: "While satellite imagery and deep learning have advanced automated fire detection, many existing approaches remain limited in accurately segmenting small-scale and irregular fire patches.
  Instance 2: urn:contentItem:6H3J-8083-S86J-437W-00000-00Researchers at Universiti Kebangsaan Malaysia Report Research in Engineering (Satellite-Based Forest Fire Mapping Using Group and Shuffle Network Embeddings)2025-10-31T00:00:00Z2025-11-03T19:29:27ZLexisNexisENGINEERINGResearchers at Universiti Kebangsaan Malaysia Report Research in Engineering (Satellite-Based Forest Fire Mapping Using Group and Shuffle Network Embeddings)2025 OCT 31 (NewsRx) -- By a News Reporter-Staff News Editor at Engineering Daily News -- Investigators publish new report on engineering. According to news originating from Bangi, Malaysia, by NewsRx editors, the research stated, "Forest fire mapping plays a vital role in environmental monitoring and disaster response."  Financial supporters for this research include Ministry of Higher Education, Malaysia, Through The Fundamental Research Grant Scheme; Universiti Kebangsaan Malaysia Through Dana Padanan Kolaborasi-geran Pembiayaan Sepadan. The news journalists obtained a quote from the research from Universiti Kebangsaan Malaysia: "While satellite imagery and deep learning have advanced automated fire detection, many existing approaches remain limited in accurately segmenting small-scale and irregular fire patches. The purpose of this study is to develop and evaluate GSDABNet, a novel deep semantic segmentation architecture for improved delineation of wildfire regions using Landsat-8 imagery.
  Instance 3: The methodological workflow includes preprocessing Landsat-8 imagery by selecting SWIR-1, SWIR-2, and Blue bands, building the proposed encoder-decoder framework with GS and DAB modules, and training on a publicly available global wildfire dataset. Model evaluation was performed using accuracy, precision, recall, F1-score, and mean Intersection over Union (mIoU), with additional ablation studies on GS placement, group size, and shuffle permutations to assess architectural contributions. Results show that the optimal configuration two groups with a (0,1,2,4,3) shuffle applied after the fifth DAB block achieved an mIoU of 0.6476, accuracy of 0.9957, and F1-score of 0.7201, outperforming multiple state-of-the-art benchmark models."  According to the news reporters, the research concluded: "These findings confirm GSDABNet as a highly accurate and computationally efficient framework for wildfire segmentation, contributing to improved early detection, effective risk mitigation, and sustainable forest management."  For more information on this research see: Satellite-Based Forest Fire Mapping Using Group and Shuffle Network Embeddings. IEEE Access, 2025,13():178387-178399. (IEEE Access - http://ieeexplore.ieee.org/servlet/opac?punumber=6287639).
  Instance 4: Keywords for this news article include: Universiti Kebangsaan Malaysia, Bangi, Malaysia, Asia, Engineering. According to news reporting from Ottawa, Canada, by NewsRx journalists, research stated, "Given the critical importance of timely forest fire detection to mitigate environmental and socio-economic consequences, this research aims to achieve high detection accuracy while maintaining real-time operational efficiency, with a particular focus on minimizing computational complexity."  The news reporters obtained a quote from the research from Research &amp; Development Department: "We propose a novel framework that systematically integrates normalization, feature selection, adaptive oversampling, and classifier optimization to enhance detection performance while minimizing computational overhead. The evaluation is conducted using three distinct Canadian forest fire datasets: Alberta Forest Fire (AFF), British Columbia Forest Fire (BCFF), and Saskatchewan Forest Fire (SFF). Initial classifier benchmarking identified the best-performing tree-based model, followed by normalization and feature selection optimization. Next, four oversampling methods were evaluated to address class imbalance.
  Instance 4: Next, four oversampling methods were evaluated to address class imbalance. An ablation study quantified the contribution of each module to overall performance. Our targeted, stepwise strategy eliminated the need for exhaustive model searches, reducing computational cost by 97.75% without compromising accuracy."  According to the news editors, the research concluded: "Experimental results demonstrate substantial improvements in F1-score, AFF (from 69.12% to 82.75%), BCFF (61.95% to 77.91%), and SFF (90.03% to 96.18%) alongside notable reductions in False Negative Rates compared to baseline models."  For more information on this research see: A Systematic Machine Learning Methodology for Enhancing Accuracy and Reducing Computational Complexity in Forest Fire Detection. Fire, 2025,8(9):341. (Fire - https://www.mdpi.com/journal/fire).

The news journalists obtained a quote from the research from Prince of Songkla University: "While prevention and suppression of forest fires are crucial components of a forest management plan, it is of paramount importance to support decisions with accurate and tangible information. Geospatial data have been a useful source in this aspect, and various techniques have been proposed to define the zonation of forest fire risk in fire-prone areas. In this study, we classify and map forest fire risk in a peat swamp forest in Khreng sub-district, Thailand. Geospatial, climatic, and topographic data (namely elevation, slope, rainfall, land use/land cover, normalized difference vegetation index, and proximity to rivers, settlements, and roads) are fed into the analytic hierarchy process (AHP) and Geographical Information System (GIS) methods to map the area into five fire risk categories.
  Instance 4: According to news originating from Songkhla, Thailand, by NewsRx editors, the research stated, "Wildfires are a main reason of environmental changes in natural ecosystems."  The news journalists obtained a quote from the research from Prince of Songkla University: "While prevention and suppression of forest fires are crucial components of a forest management plan, it is of paramount importance to support decisions with accurate and tangible information. Geospatial data have been a useful source in this aspect, and various techniques have been proposed to define the zonation of forest fire risk in fire-prone areas. In this study, we classify and map forest fire risk in a peat swamp forest in Khreng sub-district, Thailand. Geospatial, climatic, and topographic data (namely elevation, slope, rainfall, land use/land cover, normalized difference vegetation index, and proximity to rivers, settlements, and roads) are fed into the analytic hierarchy process (AHP) and Geographical Information System (GIS) methods to map the area into five fire risk categories. The results are validated based on 70 historic fire events.
  Instance 5: Geospatial, climatic, and topographic data (namely elevation, slope, rainfall, land use/land cover, normalized difference vegetation index, and proximity to rivers, settlements, and roads) are fed into the analytic hierarchy process (AHP) and Geographical Information System (GIS) methods to map the area into five fire risk categories. The results are validated based on 70 historic fire events. About 88.57% of the ground truth fire incidents occurred at locations characterized by our assessment as very high risk class and 11.43% in the high risk class."  According to the news reporters, the research concluded: "It is suggested that the synergy of geospatial data and GIS and AHP techniques yields useful and accurate fire zone maps, which may aid addressing future fire prevention measures and forest management of fire-prone areas."  For more information on this research see: The synergistic use of AHP and GIS to assess factors driving forest fire potential in a peat swamp forest in Thailand. Open Geosciences, 2025,17(1):741-6.   Instance 1: urn:contentItem:6GRN-SV73-RXRC-J1H1-00000-00Arequipa: Forest fire affects natural grasslands on Misti volcano2025-09-14T00:00:00Z2025-11-03T19:29:27ZLexisNexisArequipa: Forest fire affects natural grasslands on Misti volcanoA forest fire on the slopes of the Misti volcano, in the district of Miraflores, has been registered since Saturday morning, with the possible causes still under investigation. This fact became more notorious in the evening hours due to the fact that the fire can be seen from different districts of the city.According to the Regional Emergency Operations Center (Coer) Arequipa, this fire was reported at 11:45 hours, with no personal injuries or damage to life and health of people, but it did affect vegetation cover.Due to the topographic conditions, control efforts were complicated in the afternoon hours. The Disaster Risk Management Manager of the Regional Government of Arequipa, Jos Luis Barrezueta, informed that they are still waiting for the report from the Provincial Municipality of Arequipa regarding the number of hectares affected.Similarly, it was indicated that actions to control this forest fire are being coordinated with the District Municipality of Miraflores, the District Municipality of Chiguata and the Provincial Municipality of Arequipa, while the National Forest and Wildlife Service (SERFOR) is monitoring the effects on flora and fauna.The authorities asked the population to remain calm and follow the recommendations while the fire is being extinguished.CENFEN-73100692CENFEN2025urn:contentItem:6GRN-SV73-RXRC-J1H1-00000-004436072025-09-15Copyright 2025 Content Engine, LLC.All Rights ReservedCopyright 2025 CE Noticias Financieras All Rights ReservedCE Noticias Financieras EnglishSeptember 14, 2025 SundayNewspaperNewspapersENGLISHST000D1DRNEGATIVE NEWSSTX001500RISK MANAGEMENTSTX001009FOREST FIRESSTX001922ACCIDENTS &amp;   Instance 2: urn:contentItem:6GYP-T9F3-RV32-J221-00000-00University of Delhi Researchers Provide New Data on Artificial Neural Networks (Assessing forest fire vulnerability using artificial neural networks in Almora district, Uttarakhand, India)2025-10-13T00:00:00Z2025-11-03T19:29:27ZLexisNexisARTIFICIAL NEURAL NETWORKSUniversity of Delhi Researchers Provide New Data on Artificial Neural Networks (Assessing forest fire vulnerability using artificial neural networks in Almora district, Uttarakhand, India)2025 OCT 13 (NewsRx) -- By a News Reporter-Staff News Editor at Network Daily News -- New research on artificial neural networks is the subject of a new report. According to news reporting out of the University of Delhi by NewsRx editors, research stated, "Forests are vital to terrestrial ecosystems and they offer essential services for climate regulation and human welfare. However, the increasing trend in forest fires poses a significant threat to these ecosystems."  Our news editors obtained a quote from the research from University of Delhi: "This study aims to map and assess forest fire vulnerability zones within Almora district, Uttarakhand, India, using geospatial technologies and the Artificial Neural Network (ANN) technique. Twelve environmental indicators related to forest fire vulnerability, including elevation, slope, land use/land cover (LULC), Normalized Difference Vegetation Index (NDVI), Vegetation Health Index (VHI), temperature, precipitation, humidity, wind speed, Land Surface Temperature (LST), and distance from settlements and roads, were considered. The study revealed that a strip running from northern to southern Almora, including Someshwar, Dwarahat, and Ranikhet, is highly vulnerable to forest fires.
  Instance 3: According to news reporting out of the University of Delhi by NewsRx editors, research stated, "Forests are vital to terrestrial ecosystems and they offer essential services for climate regulation and human welfare. However, the increasing trend in forest fires poses a significant threat to these ecosystems."  Our news editors obtained a quote from the research from University of Delhi: "This study aims to map and assess forest fire vulnerability zones within Almora district, Uttarakhand, India, using geospatial technologies and the Artificial Neural Network (ANN) technique. Twelve environmental indicators related to forest fire vulnerability, including elevation, slope, land use/land cover (LULC), Normalized Difference Vegetation Index (NDVI), Vegetation Health Index (VHI), temperature, precipitation, humidity, wind speed, Land Surface Temperature (LST), and distance from settlements and roads, were considered. The study revealed that a strip running from northern to southern Almora, including Someshwar, Dwarahat, and Ranikhet, is highly vulnerable to forest fires. This region is characterized by moderate to high elevation, a moderate to steep slope, and well-connected roads and settlements, particularly in Dwarahat and Ranikhet tehsils.
  Instance 4: However, the increasing trend in forest fires poses a significant threat to these ecosystems."  Our news editors obtained a quote from the research from University of Delhi: "This study aims to map and assess forest fire vulnerability zones within Almora district, Uttarakhand, India, using geospatial technologies and the Artificial Neural Network (ANN) technique. Twelve environmental indicators related to forest fire vulnerability, including elevation, slope, land use/land cover (LULC), Normalized Difference Vegetation Index (NDVI), Vegetation Health Index (VHI), temperature, precipitation, humidity, wind speed, Land Surface Temperature (LST), and distance from settlements and roads, were considered. The study revealed that a strip running from northern to southern Almora, including Someshwar, Dwarahat, and Ranikhet, is highly vulnerable to forest fires. This region is characterized by moderate to high elevation, a moderate to steep slope, and well-connected roads and settlements, particularly in Dwarahat and Ranikhet tehsils. The central and southern parts of Almora also exhibit good road connectivity, dense human settlements, and receive moderate to low precipitation, all of which contribute to a higher fire risk.
  Instance 5: This region is characterized by moderate to high elevation, a moderate to steep slope, and well-connected roads and settlements, particularly in Dwarahat and Ranikhet tehsils. The central and southern parts of Almora also exhibit good road connectivity, dense human settlements, and receive moderate to low precipitation, all of which contribute to a higher fire risk. In contrast, the eastern and western parts of Almora, comprising northern Sult, northern Bhikiyasain, and Banoli tehsils, are significantly less vulnerable to forest fires."  According to the news editors, the research concluded: "These areas have moderate slopes, low to moderate elevation, higher precipitation in the eastern parts, and lower precipitation in the western parts, making them comparatively less prone to fire incidents. Validation through the Receiver Operating Characteristic (ROC) curve confirmed the accuracy of the model, with an 82% area under the curve."  For more information on this research see: Assessing forest fire vulnerability using artificial neural networks in Almora district, Uttarakhand, India. Journal of the Bulgarian Geographical Society, 2025,53():67-86.

Between July and November of that year, 340 fires were reported, destroying 2,274 hectares of vegetation.The FireDepartment attributed 99% of the fires to humanaction.

  Instance 1: urn:contentItem:6GS3-RCC3-RS40-Y3JR-00000-00Forest fire affects Conunhueno hill in Padre Las Casas2025-09-16T00:00:00Z2025-11-03T19:29:27ZLexisNexisForest fire affects Conunhueno hill in Padre Las CasasA violent forest fire is affecting the Conunhueno hill, in the commune of Padre Las Casas, in the Araucana Region.According to preliminary information, the fire in the vegetation of the area started around 9:00 p.m., prompting the deployment of firefighters to combat the flames.The organization deployed a total of five companies, which have had difficulties in their work, due to the problems of access to the affected place, where it is not possible to enter by vehicle.Captain Eduardo Azcar, of the 4th Temuco Fire Company, said that "the first forest fire alarm was activated due to the great extension of the fire in the scrubland, which is difficult to access. Bai Zhonghua, member of the Party Committee and Deputy Director of the Provincial Emergency Management Department, attended the opening ceremony and delivered a speech.Bai Zhonghua pointed out that since last year, with the concerted efforts of the entire system and leveraging the opportunity of additional treasury bonds, a comprehensive monitoring and perception, early warning and response, command and dispatch, and rescue equipment system covering the entire region, all types of disasters, and the entire supply chain has been basically established. This has led to a comprehensive and leapfrog improvement in the prevention, mitigation, and rescue systems and capacity building at the provincial, municipal, county, township, and village levels.
  Instance 3: Bai Zhonghua, member of the Party Committee and Deputy Director of the Provincial Emergency Management Department, attended the opening ceremony and delivered a speech.Bai Zhonghua pointed out that since last year, with the concerted efforts of the entire system and leveraging the opportunity of additional treasury bonds, a comprehensive monitoring and perception, early warning and response, command and dispatch, and rescue equipment system covering the entire region, all types of disasters, and the entire supply chain has been basically established. This has led to a comprehensive and leapfrog improvement in the prevention, mitigation, and rescue systems and capacity building at the provincial, municipal, county, township, and village levels. In the field of forest fire prevention and control, the problems of lack of monitoring methods, inaccurate early warnings, and untimely detection have been completely resolved. Firefighting methods have been completely transformed from wind-driven extinguishing to a combination of wind and water, with water as the primary method. This has played a vital role in ensuring and supporting the victory in the battle against forest fires last winter and this spring, and has laid a solid foundation for promoting the "five-pronged expansion" of forest fire prevention and control work during the 15th Five-Year Plan period.Bai Zhonghua emphasized that all levels of government must integrate forest fire prevention and control into the grassroots emergency response system and capacity building, comprehensively consider, design, and promote them as a whole.

According to news originating from Hebei, People's Republic of China, by NewsRx correspondents, research stated, "Forests not only provide important resources for the earth, but also play an important role in maintaining ecological balance. Once forest fires occur, they will pose a serious threat to human beings." The early forest fire smoke flame target is small and the dynamic change is difficult to identify. In this study, a forest fire dataset is first constructed, and an early forest fire detection model, YOLO-MC, based on YOLOV8, is proposed.
  Instance 3: According to news originating from Hebei, People's Republic of China, by NewsRx correspondents, research stated, "Forests not only provide important resources for the earth, but also play an important role in maintaining ecological balance. Once forest fires occur, they will pose a serious threat to human beings."  The news reporters obtained a quote from the research from North China Institute of Science and Technology: "As a convenient and high-definition remote sensing equipment, unmanned aerial vehicle provides effective support for forest fire monitoring. The early forest fire smoke flame target is small and the dynamic change is difficult to identify. In this study, a forest fire dataset is first constructed, and an early forest fire detection model, YOLO-MC, based on YOLOV8, is proposed. Lightweight backbone network MobileNetV3 is used to replace the original backbone.
  Instance 4: Once forest fires occur, they will pose a serious threat to human beings."  The news reporters obtained a quote from the research from North China Institute of Science and Technology: "As a convenient and high-definition remote sensing equipment, unmanned aerial vehicle provides effective support for forest fire monitoring. The early forest fire smoke flame target is small and the dynamic change is difficult to identify. In this study, a forest fire dataset is first constructed, and an early forest fire detection model, YOLO-MC, based on YOLOV8, is proposed. Lightweight backbone network MobileNetV3 is used to replace the original backbone. Convolutional block attention module attention mechanism is added to make the model pay more attention to local information connection.
  Instance 5: Bidirectional feature pyramid network and small target layer are introduced to dynamically assign weights to identify small targets. Dynamic head is used to improve the flexibility of model inspection. Generalized intersection over union is used as a loss function to improve the accuracy of target positioning."  According to the news editors, the research concluded: "Compared with the benchmark model, the accuracy and average accuracy of YOLO-MC are increased by 4.3 and 3.6%, respectively, and the number of parameters is reduced by 2 x 104, which indicates that YOLO-MC can improve the identification efficiency of early forest fires and realize the early detection of forest fires at the same time. It helps in identifying forest fires as early as possible and has certain practical significance."  For more information on this research see: YOLO-MC: An algorithm for early forest fire recognition based on drone image. Open Geosciences, 2025,17(1):1-12.
  Instance 6: Dynamic head is used to improve the flexibility of model inspection. Generalized intersection over union is used as a loss function to improve the accuracy of target positioning."  According to the news editors, the research concluded: "Compared with the benchmark model, the accuracy and average accuracy of YOLO-MC are increased by 4.3 and 3.6%, respectively, and the number of parameters is reduced by 2 x 104, which indicates that YOLO-MC can improve the identification efficiency of early forest fires and realize the early detection of forest fires at the same time. According to news reporting out of Harbin, People's Republic of China, by NewsRx editors, research stated, "Forest fires pose severe ecological, climatic, and socio-economic threats, destroying habitats and emitting greenhouse gases. Early and timely warning is particularly challenging because fires often originate from small-scale, low-temperature ignition sources."  Financial supporters for this research include National Key Research And Development Program of China; Fundamental Research Funds For The Central Universities. The news correspondents obtained a quote from the research from Northeast Forestry University: "Traditional monitoring approaches primarily rely on single-source satellite imagery and empirical threshold algorithms, and most forest fire monitoring tasks remain human-driven.
  Instance 3: According to news reporting out of Harbin, People's Republic of China, by NewsRx editors, research stated, "Forest fires pose severe ecological, climatic, and socio-economic threats, destroying habitats and emitting greenhouse gases. Early and timely warning is particularly challenging because fires often originate from small-scale, low-temperature ignition sources."  Financial supporters for this research include National Key Research And Development Program of China; Fundamental Research Funds For The Central Universities. The news correspondents obtained a quote from the research from Northeast Forestry University: "Traditional monitoring approaches primarily rely on single-source satellite imagery and empirical threshold algorithms, and most forest fire monitoring tasks remain human-driven. Existing frameworks have yet to effectively integrate multiple data sources and detection algorithms, lacking the capability to provide continuous, automated, and generalizable fire monitoring across diverse fire scenarios. To address these challenges, this study first improves multiple monitoring algorithms for forest fire detection, including a statistically enhanced automatic thresholding method; data augmentation to expand the U-Net deep learning dataset; and the application of a freeze-unfreeze transfer learning strategy to the U-Net transfer model.
  Instance 4: The news correspondents obtained a quote from the research from Northeast Forestry University: "Traditional monitoring approaches primarily rely on single-source satellite imagery and empirical threshold algorithms, and most forest fire monitoring tasks remain human-driven. Existing frameworks have yet to effectively integrate multiple data sources and detection algorithms, lacking the capability to provide continuous, automated, and generalizable fire monitoring across diverse fire scenarios. To address these challenges, this study first improves multiple monitoring algorithms for forest fire detection, including a statistically enhanced automatic thresholding method; data augmentation to expand the U-Net deep learning dataset; and the application of a freeze-unfreeze transfer learning strategy to the U-Net transfer model. Multiple algorithms are systematically evaluated across varying fire scales, showing that the improved automatic threshold method achieves the best performance on GF-4 imagery with an F-score of 0.915 (95% CI: 0.8725-0.9524), while the U-Net deep learning algorithm yields the highest F-score of 0.921 (95% CI: 0.8537-0.9739) on Landsat 8 imagery. All methods demonstrate robust performance and generalizability across diverse scenarios.
  Instance 5: All methods demonstrate robust performance and generalizability across diverse scenarios. Second, data-driven scheduling technology is developed to automatically initiate preprocessing and fire detection tasks, significantly reducing fire discovery time. Finally, an integrated framework of multi-source remote sensing data, advanced detection algorithms, and a user-friendly visualization interface is proposed."  According to the news reporters, the research concluded: "This framework enables all-weather, fully automated forest fire monitoring and early warning, facilitating dynamic tracking of fire evolution and precise fire line localization through the cross-application of heterogeneous data sources. The framework's effectiveness and practicality are validated through wildfire cases in two regions of Yunnan Province, offering scalable technical support for improving early detection of and rapid response to forest fires."  For more information on this research see: All-Weather Forest Fire Automatic Monitoring and Early Warning Application Based on Multi-Source Remote Sensing Data: Case Study of Yunnan. Fire, 2025,8(9):344.
  Instance 6: Second, data-driven scheduling technology is developed to automatically initiate preprocessing and fire detection tasks, significantly reducing fire discovery time. Finally, an integrated framework of multi-source remote sensing data, advanced detection algorithms, and a user-friendly visualization interface is proposed." The framework's effectiveness and practicality are validated through wildfire cases in two regions of Yunnan Province, offering scalable technical support for improving early detection of and rapid response to forest fires." Fire, 2025,8(9):344. (Fire - https://www.mdpi.com/journal/fire).

New Findings on Engineering Described by Investigators at Dalian University of Technology (A New Weighted Rough Set and Improved Bp Neural Network Method for Predicting Forest Fires) [12]
  Instance 1: urn:contentItem:6H3B-9H33-RW0T-82RM-00000-00New Findings on Engineering Described by Investigators at Dalian University of Technology (A New Weighted Rough Set and Improved Bp Neural Network Method for Predicting Forest Fires)2025-10-30T00:00:00Z2025-11-03T19:29:27ZLexisNexisENGINEERINGNew Findings on Engineering Described by Investigators at Dalian University of Technology (A New Weighted Rough Set and Improved Bp Neural Network Method for Predicting Forest Fires)2025 OCT 30 (NewsRx) -- By a News Reporter-Staff News Editor at Disease Prevention Daily -- Investigators publish new report on Engineering. According to news originating from Liaoning, People's Republic of China, by NewsRx correspondents, research stated, "To solve the quality problems of redundant risk elements, data imbalance, and noisy samples, which are commonly found in forest fire datasets, and to further improve the accuracy of forest fire risk prediction. In this paper, a forest fire prediction method is proposed, which combines a probability-weighted rough set attribute reduction (PWRS-AR) strategy with a particle swarm optimization improved BP neural network (PSO-I-BPNN) for forest fire prediction."  Financial support for this research came from National Natural Science Foundation of China (NSFC).

In this paper, a forest fire prediction method is proposed, which combines a probability-weighted rough set attribute reduction (PWRS-AR) strategy with a particle swarm optimization improved BP neural network (PSO-I-BPNN) for forest fire prediction."  Financial support for this research came from National Natural Science Foundation of China (NSFC).   Instance 3: urn:contentItem:6H3B-9H33-RW0T-82RM-00000-00New Findings on Engineering Described by Investigators at Dalian University of Technology (A New Weighted Rough Set and Improved Bp Neural Network Method for Predicting Forest Fires)2025-10-30T00:00:00Z2025-11-03T19:29:27ZLexisNexisENGINEERINGNew Findings on Engineering Described by Investigators at Dalian University of Technology (A New Weighted Rough Set and Improved Bp Neural Network Method for Predicting Forest Fires)2025 OCT 30 (NewsRx) -- By a News Reporter-Staff News Editor at Disease Prevention Daily -- Investigators publish new report on Engineering. According to news originating from Liaoning, People's Republic of China, by NewsRx correspondents, research stated, "To solve the quality problems of redundant risk elements, data imbalance, and noisy samples, which are commonly found in forest fire datasets, and to further improve the accuracy of forest fire risk prediction. In this paper, a forest fire prediction method is proposed, which combines a probability-weighted rough set attribute reduction (PWRS-AR) strategy with a particle swarm optimization improved BP neural network (PSO-I-BPNN) for forest fire prediction."  Financial support for this research came from National Natural Science Foundation of China (NSFC). Our news journalists obtained a quote from the research from the Dalian University of Technology, "Firstly, a probabilistic weighted rough set attribute reduction method is designed to effectively eliminate non-critical and redundant features in the dataset and simplify the input space of the neural network. Subsequently, a particle swarm optimization (PSO) algorithm is employed to refine the BP neural network (BPNN), aiming to elevate both the precision and efficiency of forest fire prediction.
  Instance 4: In this paper, a forest fire prediction method is proposed, which combines a probability-weighted rough set attribute reduction (PWRS-AR) strategy with a particle swarm optimization improved BP neural network (PSO-I-BPNN) for forest fire prediction."  Financial support for this research came from National Natural Science Foundation of China (NSFC). Our news journalists obtained a quote from the research from the Dalian University of Technology, "Firstly, a probabilistic weighted rough set attribute reduction method is designed to effectively eliminate non-critical and redundant features in the dataset and simplify the input space of the neural network. Subsequently, a particle swarm optimization (PSO) algorithm is employed to refine the BP neural network (BPNN), aiming to elevate both the precision and efficiency of forest fire prediction. To validate the method's effectiveness, experiments are conducted on three representative forest fire datasets."  According to the news editors, the research concluded: "The results show that compared with the traditional machine learning prediction methods, the proposed forest fire prediction model achieves a significant improvement in prediction accuracy and is more suitable for early warning and disaster prevention and mitigation strategies in forest fire-prone areas."  This research has been peer-reviewed. For more information on this research see: A New Weighted Rough Set and Improved Bp Neural Network Method for Predicting Forest Fires.
  Instance 5: Our news journalists obtained a quote from the research from the Dalian University of Technology, "Firstly, a probabilistic weighted rough set attribute reduction method is designed to effectively eliminate non-critical and redundant features in the dataset and simplify the input space of the neural network. Subsequently, a particle swarm optimization (PSO) algorithm is employed to refine the BP neural network (BPNN), aiming to elevate both the precision and efficiency of forest fire prediction. To validate the method's effectiveness, experiments are conducted on three representative forest fire datasets."  According to the news editors, the research concluded: "The results show that compared with the traditional machine learning prediction methods, the proposed forest fire prediction model achieves a significant improvement in prediction accuracy and is more suitable for early warning and disaster prevention and mitigation strategies in forest fire-prone areas."  This research has been peer-reviewed. For more information on this research see: A New Weighted Rough Set and Improved Bp Neural Network Method for Predicting Forest Fires. New forest fire hits Quito this September 2nd [8]
  Instance 1: urn:contentItem:6GN4-5F03-S5NX-F0K7-00000-00New forest fire hits Quito this September 2nd2025-09-02T00:00:00Z2025-11-03T19:29:27ZLexisNexisNew forest fire hits Quito this September 2ndThe Emergency Service ECU911 informed on Tuesday, September 2, about a new forest fire registered in a sector of Quito.???? Forest fire in La Betania sectorECU911 reported that the forest fire was verified through video surveillance devices at 10:30 today, in the La Betania sector, in Luis Tufio and Gualaquiza streets, in the north of Quito.From the 911 Operational Room, the mobilization of the Quito Fire Department contingent was coordinated in a timely manner.Personnel of this emergency institution went immediately and found the flames on a hillside, so they activated the work of smothering the flames to prevent them from consuming all the vegetation on the hillside.The fire departmentresponded with personnel and a firefighting unit.In spite of the smoke generated by the fire, the traffic is still open on this road; however, it is recommended to drive with caution, as there is smoke and a Fire Department unit on the road.Remember to call 911 immediately if you detect a column of smoke or a fire.???? High daytime temperatures may contribute to the formation of forest firesThe Metropolitan EOC warns about the risk of heat stroke and dehydration, especially in vulnerable groups due to high daytime temperatures.
  Instance 2: urn:contentItem:6GN4-5F03-S5NX-F0K7-00000-00New forest fire hits Quito this September 2nd2025-09-02T00:00:00Z2025-11-03T19:29:27ZLexisNexisNew forest fire hits Quito this September 2ndThe Emergency Service ECU911 informed on Tuesday, September 2, about a new forest fire registered in a sector of Quito.???? Forest fire in La Betania sectorECU911 reported that the forest fire was verified through video surveillance devices at 10:30 today, in the La Betania sector, in Luis Tufio and Gualaquiza streets, in the north of Quito.From the 911 Operational Room, the mobilization of the Quito Fire Department contingent was coordinated in a timely manner.Personnel of this emergency institution went immediately and found the flames on a hillside, so they activated the work of smothering the flames to prevent them from consuming all the vegetation on the hillside.The fire departmentresponded with personnel and a firefighting unit.In spite of the smoke generated by the fire, the traffic is still open on this road; however, it is recommended to drive with caution, as there is smoke and a Fire Department unit on the road.Remember to call 911 immediately if you detect a column of smoke or a fire.???? High daytime temperatures may contribute to the formation of forest firesThe Metropolitan EOC warns about the risk of heat stroke and dehydration, especially in vulnerable groups due to high daytime temperatures. Likewise, there may be higher consumption of water and electricity due to the use of cooling systems.With these conditions, the probability of forest fires increases in some sectors, take precautions and do not burn in dry areas or light sparks.Ultraviolet radiation remains at extremely high levels, so always use sunscreen.Wear clothing that covers your skin, so you will be protected from radiation and the sun.Stay hydratedKeep rooms cool and ventilatedPay more attention to children and elderly peopleWe recommend youCENFEN-72670974CENFEN2025urn:contentItem:6GN4-5F03-S5NX-F0K7-00000-004436072025-09-03Copyright 2025 Content Engine, LLC.All Rights ReservedCopyright 2025 CE Noticias Financieras All Rights ReservedCE Noticias Financieras EnglishSeptember 2, 2025 TuesdayNewspaperNewspapersENGLISHCC000DR88METROPOLITAN BANK HOLDING CORPNAICS522110 COMMERCIAL BANKINGSIC6029 COMMERCIAL BANKS, NECMCB (NYSE)Quito Cuerpo de Bomberos Quito incendio incendio forestal Sntesis NoticiosaST000DKTFSURVEILLANCESTX001009FOREST FIRESST000D3TVWATER CONSUMPTIONN624230GMEMERGENCY MEDICAL SERVICESN922160CCFIRE DEPARTMENTSST000DLZBEMERGENCY SERVICESSTX000726FIRESSTX001659SURVEILLANCE TECHNOLOGYST000CYFWHEAT STRESS DISORDERSST000A6OASENIOR CITIZENSSTX001900ENERGY &amp;   Instance 4: WE RECOMMEND YOUSin Guin | Phillip Butters in LR In terms of fauna, the species affected are Andean foxes, partridges, eagles, small birds, lizards, wild guinea pigs and other rodents. It is worth mentioning that, although these animals have not been consumed by the fire, their habitat has been destroyed, so they end up displaced. The Serfor official pointed out that the exact number of hectares devastated by the forest fire on Saturday and Sunday has not yet been calculated. Only in the first hours of the fire, 47 hectares were estimated, but the figure increased as the hours went by. Invaders are suspected of causing the fire.

According to the entity, the fire was controlled by midday, but it is still being monitored.   Instance 4: According to news originating from Madhya Pradesh, India, by NewsRx correspondents, research stated, "India has been witnessing a rise in forest fire frequency and intensity due to climate change factors such as increasing temperatures, erratic rainfall, and prolonged droughts. These changes pose severe risks to biodiversity, carbon stocks, and forest-dependent communities, making assessing the climate change-forest fire relationship essential."  Financial support for this research came from King Saud University. Our news journalists obtained a quote from the research from the Indian Institute of Technology (IIT) Indore, "This systematic review synthesizes evidence on climate change-induced forest fires in India, their ecological and socio-economic impacts, and current adaptation measures. Forests cover 21.67% of India's land, and 36% are prone to forest fire incidents. The literature revealed a strong correlation between increasing temperatures and increased forest fire events, especially in the Western Ghats, Himalayas, Northeastern region, and central India.
  Instance 5: These changes pose severe risks to biodiversity, carbon stocks, and forest-dependent communities, making assessing the climate change-forest fire relationship essential."  Financial support for this research came from King Saud University. Our news journalists obtained a quote from the research from the Indian Institute of Technology (IIT) Indore, "This systematic review synthesizes evidence on climate change-induced forest fires in India, their ecological and socio-economic impacts, and current adaptation measures. Forests cover 21.67% of India's land, and 36% are prone to forest fire incidents. The literature revealed a strong correlation between increasing temperatures and increased forest fire events, especially in the Western Ghats, Himalayas, Northeastern region, and central India. Major ecological impacts comprise habitat loss, soil degradation, and increasing emissions of greenhouse gases, while socio-economic consequences vary from livelihood difficulties to health issues.
  Instance 6: Our news journalists obtained a quote from the research from the Indian Institute of Technology (IIT) Indore, "This systematic review synthesizes evidence on climate change-induced forest fires in India, their ecological and socio-economic impacts, and current adaptation measures. Forests cover 21.67% of India's land, and 36% are prone to forest fire incidents. The literature revealed a strong correlation between increasing temperatures and increased forest fire events, especially in the Western Ghats, Himalayas, Northeastern region, and central India. Major ecological impacts comprise habitat loss, soil degradation, and increasing emissions of greenhouse gases, while socio-economic consequences vary from livelihood difficulties to health issues. Despite technological advancements in early warning systems, community involvement, policy integration, and resource limitations remain.
  Instance 7: Major ecological impacts comprise habitat loss, soil degradation, and increasing emissions of greenhouse gases, while socio-economic consequences vary from livelihood difficulties to health issues. Despite technological advancements in early warning systems, community involvement, policy integration, and resource limitations remain. The study demonstrates the necessity for climate-resilient forest fire management by promoting community-based adaptation, upgrading forest fire monitoring networks, and integrating forest fire risk assessment into climate action and Sustainable Development Goal-13 (SDG-13) plans are essential."  According to the news editors, the research concluded: "Addressing India's forest fire risk calls for an integrated approach combining scientific findings, reforms to policy, and community involvement, which is crucial for safeguarding India's ecosystems and vulnerable populations in a changing climatic scenario."  For more information on this research see: Forest Fires and Climate Change In India: Impacts, Adaptive Strategies, and Pathways for Climate Action (Sustainable Development Goal-13). Environmental Sciences Europe, 2025;37(1). Environmental Sciences Europe can be contacted at: Springer, One New York Plaza, Suite 4600, New York, Ny, United States.

Korea Water Resources Corporation Researchers Describe Advances in Environmental Science (Interception reduction from deforestation and forest fire increases large-scale fluvial flooding risk) [5]
  Instance 1: urn:contentItem:6H1M-HF73-RSV0-53HH-00000-00Korea Water Resources Corporation Researchers Describe Advances in Environmental Science (Interception reduction from deforestation and forest fire increases large-scale fluvial flooding risk)2025-10-22T00:00:00Z2025-11-03T19:29:27ZLexisNexisENVIRONMENT - ENVIRONMENTAL SCIENCEKorea Water Resources Corporation Researchers Describe Advances in Environmental Science (Interception reduction from deforestation and forest fire increases large-scale fluvial flooding risk)2025 OCT 22 (NewsRx) -- By a News Reporter-Staff News Editor at Climate Change Daily News -- Data detailed on environmental science have been presented. According to news originating from the Korea Water Resources Corporation by NewsRx editors, the research stated, "Catastrophic flooding has been noted to occur with greater frequency following deforestation, but limited observations have been available to test this connection over large spatial scales."  Our news journalists obtained a quote from the research from Korea Water Resources Corporation: "Here we used the data of mega forest fires impacting a region of 25,000 km2 in Australia exhibiting rapid loss in forest canopy, where the runoff generation has been carefully observed with minimum anthropogenic influences for more than half a century. This provides a unique opportunity to assess the impact of the forest canopy loss on large-scale fluvial flooding.
  Instance 2: urn:contentItem:6H1M-HF73-RSV0-53HH-00000-00Korea Water Resources Corporation Researchers Describe Advances in Environmental Science (Interception reduction from deforestation and forest fire increases large-scale fluvial flooding risk)2025-10-22T00:00:00Z2025-11-03T19:29:27ZLexisNexisENVIRONMENT - ENVIRONMENTAL SCIENCEKorea Water Resources Corporation Researchers Describe Advances in Environmental Science (Interception reduction from deforestation and forest fire increases large-scale fluvial flooding risk)2025 OCT 22 (NewsRx) -- By a News Reporter-Staff News Editor at Climate Change Daily News -- Data detailed on environmental science have been presented. According to news originating from the Korea Water Resources Corporation by NewsRx editors, the research stated, "Catastrophic flooding has been noted to occur with greater frequency following deforestation, but limited observations have been available to test this connection over large spatial scales."  Our news journalists obtained a quote from the research from Korea Water Resources Corporation: "Here we used the data of mega forest fires impacting a region of 25,000 km2 in Australia exhibiting rapid loss in forest canopy, where the runoff generation has been carefully observed with minimum anthropogenic influences for more than half a century. This provides a unique opportunity to assess the impact of the forest canopy loss on large-scale fluvial flooding. A state-controlled hypothesis test, with the climate and watershed states controlled to enhance robustness, shows a statistically significant increase in annual maximum flows resulting from the forest loss treatment."  According to the news reporters, the research concluded: "The reasoning for this natural experiment is that the forest loss impact on the interception potential of forest canopy, fallen leaves, and root-zone soils in wide region could have a recognizable impact on the fluvial flood."  For more information on this research see: Interception reduction from deforestation and forest fire increases large-scale fluvial flooding risk.
  Instance 3: According to news originating from the Korea Water Resources Corporation by NewsRx editors, the research stated, "Catastrophic flooding has been noted to occur with greater frequency following deforestation, but limited observations have been available to test this connection over large spatial scales."  Our news journalists obtained a quote from the research from Korea Water Resources Corporation: "Here we used the data of mega forest fires impacting a region of 25,000 km2 in Australia exhibiting rapid loss in forest canopy, where the runoff generation has been carefully observed with minimum anthropogenic influences for more than half a century. This provides a unique opportunity to assess the impact of the forest canopy loss on large-scale fluvial flooding. A state-controlled hypothesis test, with the climate and watershed states controlled to enhance robustness, shows a statistically significant increase in annual maximum flows resulting from the forest loss treatment."  According to the news reporters, the research concluded: "The reasoning for this natural experiment is that the forest loss impact on the interception potential of forest canopy, fallen leaves, and root-zone soils in wide region could have a recognizable impact on the fluvial flood."  For more information on this research see: Interception reduction from deforestation and forest fire increases large-scale fluvial flooding risk. Trkiye's Fierce Forest Fire Reaches Residential Neighborhoods [5]
  Instance 1: urn:contentItem:6GMP-VS73-RTKJ-1155-00000-00Trkiye's Fierce Forest Fire Reaches Residential Neighborhoods2025-09-01T00:00:00Z2025-11-03T19:29:27ZLexisNexisTrkiye's Fierce Forest Fire Reaches Residential NeighborhoodsLink to ImageLink to StoryA severe forest fire in Denizli province, western Trkiye, has reached residential neighborhoods, burning houses and leading to widespread evacuations, authorities confirmed Monday.Governor Omer Faruk Coskun reported that all available resources have been deployed and firefighting efforts are ongoing to bring the blaze under control.The fire's spread into populated areas has prompted the evacuation of 84 households to safer locations, as officials prioritize public safety.Patients at Buldan Chest Diseases Hospital and its nearby annex in the Buldan district were also evacuated as a precaution due to the advancing fire. Ambulances transferred those under treatment to hospitals in Denizli's city center, and a temporary medical tent was set up near the hospital to provide urgent care.A video shared by local news platform Denizli Trafik Yasam showed flames driven by strong winds reaching residential zones, with residents fleeing in panic and trying to rescue their livestock from the fire.The forest fire started on August 27 in the Buldan district of Denizli and spread across the provincial border into neighboring Aydin. September 18, 2025: Autonomous University of Barcelona Horses, possible allies in forest fire prevention [4]
  Instance 1: urn:contentItem:6GSC-N1X3-RS4W-50W2-00000-00September 18, 2025: Autonomous University of Barcelona Horses, possible allies in forest fire prevention2025-09-19T00:00:00Z2025-11-03T19:29:32ZLexisNexisANNOUNCEMENTSSeptember 18, 2025: Autonomous University of Barcelona Horses, possible allies in forest fire preventionThe research-which included the participation of Boumort Wildland, the Miranda Foundation, the Forest Horses association, and the University of Barcelona (UB)-reveals that horses adapt their diet according to breed, environment and use. This flexibility helps them play a complementary role alongside other herbivores in sustainable fire prevention strategies, given that their grazing reduces fuel loads and maintains open landscapes. The study was co-authored by researchers from the Department of Animal and Food Science at the UAB Jordi Bartolome and Araceli Gort-Esteve."Until now research on extensive herding and forest fire prevention has focused mainly on sheep and goats, with some isolated studies done on breeds of rustic cattle.
  Instance 2: urn:contentItem:6GSC-N1X3-RS4W-50W2-00000-00September 18, 2025: Autonomous University of Barcelona Horses, possible allies in forest fire prevention2025-09-19T00:00:00Z2025-11-03T19:29:32ZLexisNexisANNOUNCEMENTSSeptember 18, 2025: Autonomous University of Barcelona Horses, possible allies in forest fire preventionThe research-which included the participation of Boumort Wildland, the Miranda Foundation, the Forest Horses association, and the University of Barcelona (UB)-reveals that horses adapt their diet according to breed, environment and use. This flexibility helps them play a complementary role alongside other herbivores in sustainable fire prevention strategies, given that their grazing reduces fuel loads and maintains open landscapes. The study was co-authored by researchers from the Department of Animal and Food Science at the UAB Jordi Bartolome and Araceli Gort-Esteve."Until now research on extensive herding and forest fire prevention has focused mainly on sheep and goats, with some isolated studies done on breeds of rustic cattle. There have been very few studies on horses within this context, since traditionally they are classified as plant grazers that have little effect on woody vegetations", explains Ariadna Nieto-Espinet, Ramon y Cajal researcher at the UdL and zooarchaeologist. "Our work is one of the first to use empirical data to analyse their potential in forest management in the Mediterannean", she adds.PermID: 5068482244Created by www.buysellsignals.com for News Bites FinanceNBPCOM-19092505511637870001104626NBPCOM2025urn:contentItem:6GSC-N1X3-RS4W-50W2-00000-004140052025-09-18Copyright 2025 Jupiter International (Australia) Pty Ltd.

September 18, 2025: Study Highlights Role of Autonomous University of Barcelona Horses in Forest Fire Management [4]
  Instance 1: urn:contentItem:6GSP-9MS3-RTDK-W31D-00000-00September 18, 2025: Study Highlights Role of Autonomous University of Barcelona Horses in Forest Fire Management2025-09-20T00:00:00Z2025-11-03T19:29:32ZLexisNexisANNOUNCEMENTSSeptember 18, 2025: Study Highlights Role of Autonomous University of Barcelona Horses in Forest Fire ManagementResearch conducted with the involvement of Boumort Wildland, the Miranda Foundation, the Forest Horses association, and the University of Barcelona (UB) indicates that horses modify their diets according to their breed, environment, and purpose. This dietary flexibility allows them to serve as valuable partners to other herbivores in sustainable strategies for fire prevention, as their grazing activity helps lower fuel loads and maintain open landscapes. The study was co-authored by Jordi Bartolome and Araceli Gort-Esteve from the Department of Animal and Food Science at the UAB.
  Instance 2: This dietary flexibility allows them to serve as valuable partners to other herbivores in sustainable strategies for fire prevention, as their grazing activity helps lower fuel loads and maintain open landscapes. The study was co-authored by Jordi Bartolome and Araceli Gort-Esteve from the Department of Animal and Food Science at the UAB. "Until now research on extensive herding and forest fire prevention has focused mainly on sheep and goats, with some isolated studies done on breeds of rustic cattle. There have been very few studies on horses within this context, since traditionally they are classified as plant grazers that have little effect on woody vegetation," states Ariadna Nieto-Espinet, a Ramon y Cajal researcher at the UdL and zooarchaeologist. "Our work is one of the first to use empirical data to analyse their potential in forest management in the Mediterranean," she further notes.PermID: 5068482244Created by www.buysellsignals.com for News Bites FinanceNBPCOM-20092509585558360001104626NBPCOM2025urn:contentItem:6GSP-9MS3-RTDK-W31D-00000-004140052025-09-19Copyright 2025 Jupiter International (Australia) Pty Ltd.

New recruits bolster firefighting resources across Victoria: FFMVic [6]
  Instance 1: urn:contentItem:6H1V-8MF3-S53W-C3T5-00000-00New recruits bolster firefighting resources across Victoria: FFMVic2025-10-23T00:00:00Z2025-11-03T19:29:32ZLexisNexisNew recruits bolster firefighting resources across Victoria: FFMVicForest Fire Management Victoria (FFMVic), Media Release, 23 October 2025Forest Fire Management Victorias (FFMVic) newest recruits are gearing up for the summer bushfire season, undertaking intensive training camps across the state.The training camps ensure seasonal forest and fire operations officers are well-prepared to respond to emergencies and carry out vital work to reduce bushfire risk.Photo: FFMVicThis summer, FFMVic is welcoming 636 seasonal firefighters who will work alongside our experienced permanent crews to help protect communities and the environment. Fourteen training camps are being held across the state over the coming weeks.Photo: FFMVicRecruits complete two weeks of classroom and field-based learning, covering topics such as fire behaviour, safety and survival techniques, fire suppression, working around aircraft, and planned burning.The camps offer hands-on experience, including operating water pumps and chainsaws, and driving specialised firefighting vehicles.Beyond emergency response, seasonal forest and fire operations officers also carry out important land management tasks such as mulching, mowing, slashing, and spraying.They help maintain fuel breaks, public land roads, trails, recreation sites, and assist with planned burns.This summer, 92 seasonal firefighters will be based in the Loddon Mallee Region, working from depots across the region.Last year, FFMVic firefighters responded to more than 1,265 bushfires across Victoria and delivered priority planned burns to help reduce the impact of future fires.Quotes attributable to Forest Fire Management Victoria Chief Fire Officer, Chris Hardman:Our seasonal forest and fire operations officers join us from diverse backgrounds, reflecting the communities we serve.They play a critical role alongside our experienced crews, responding to bushfires in some of the states most remote and challenging environments to keep communities safe.This summer, theyll be part of a team of nearly 1800 frontline personnel and 1200 accredited incident management staff.Photo: FFMVicQuotes attributable to Forest Fire Management Victoria Acting Deputy Chief Fire Officer  Loddon Mallee, Aaron GayWith an increased risk of bushfires forecast for the region, our seasonal firefighters are an important and valued addition to our firefighting resources this summer."New recruits train and work alongside our permanent firefighting crews, responding to bushfires rapidly to keep communities safe this summer.Last year, Forest Fire Management Victoria responded to 233 bushfires in the Loddon Mallee region, also delivering priority planned burns which will help reduce the impact of bushfires this summer.Photo: FFMVicPhoto: FFMVicPhoto:   Instance 2: urn:contentItem:6H1V-8MF3-S53W-C3T5-00000-00New recruits bolster firefighting resources across Victoria: FFMVic2025-10-23T00:00:00Z2025-11-03T19:29:32ZLexisNexisNew recruits bolster firefighting resources across Victoria: FFMVicForest Fire Management Victoria (FFMVic), Media Release, 23 October 2025Forest Fire Management Victorias (FFMVic) newest recruits are gearing up for the summer bushfire season, undertaking intensive training camps across the state.The training camps ensure seasonal forest and fire operations officers are well-prepared to respond to emergencies and carry out vital work to reduce bushfire risk.Photo: FFMVicThis summer, FFMVic is welcoming 636 seasonal firefighters who will work alongside our experienced permanent crews to help protect communities and the environment. Fourteen training camps are being held across the state over the coming weeks.Photo: FFMVicRecruits complete two weeks of classroom and field-based learning, covering topics such as fire behaviour, safety and survival techniques, fire suppression, working around aircraft, and planned burning.The camps offer hands-on experience, including operating water pumps and chainsaws, and driving specialised firefighting vehicles.Beyond emergency response, seasonal forest and fire operations officers also carry out important land management tasks such as mulching, mowing, slashing, and spraying.They help maintain fuel breaks, public land roads, trails, recreation sites, and assist with planned burns.This summer, 92 seasonal firefighters will be based in the Loddon Mallee Region, working from depots across the region.Last year, FFMVic firefighters responded to more than 1,265 bushfires across Victoria and delivered priority planned burns to help reduce the impact of future fires.Quotes attributable to Forest Fire Management Victoria Chief Fire Officer, Chris Hardman:Our seasonal forest and fire operations officers join us from diverse backgrounds, reflecting the communities we serve.They play a critical role alongside our experienced crews, responding to bushfires in some of the states most remote and challenging environments to keep communities safe.This summer, theyll be part of a team of nearly 1800 frontline personnel and 1200 accredited incident management staff.Photo: FFMVicQuotes attributable to Forest Fire Management Victoria Acting Deputy Chief Fire Officer  Loddon Mallee, Aaron GayWith an increased risk of bushfires forecast for the region, our seasonal firefighters are an important and valued addition to our firefighting resources this summer."New recruits train and work alongside our permanent firefighting crews, responding to bushfires rapidly to keep communities safe this summer.Last year, Forest Fire Management Victoria responded to 233 bushfires in the Loddon Mallee region, also delivering priority planned burns which will help reduce the impact of bushfires this summer.Photo: FFMVicPhoto: FFMVicPhoto: Trucks off the road ahead of summer sizzle [3]
  Instance 1: urn:contentItem:6H0J-2CW3-RSC3-923W-00000-00Trucks off the road ahead of summer sizzle2025-10-18T00:00:00Z2025-11-03T19:29:32ZLexisNexisNews6Trucks off the road ahead of summer sizzleChelsea Wilson'Our crown land firefighting fleet has been significantly impacted.'Forest Fire Management Victoria has removed hundreds of Mercedes-Benz firefighting vehicles from service due to safety concerns.After routine inspections revealed issues with the vehicles, 280 G-wagons and 59 Unimogs have been taken off the road to be checked and repaired if necessary."These repairs are being fast-tracked over the next two months," a Victorian government spokesperson said. "FFMVic is working on agreements to secure additional emergency response vehicles from other states if required."The vehicles are used by FFMVic for accessing remote terrain and have been grounded because of cracking issues with the chassis on the G-wagons.Victorian Nationals leader Danny O'Brien slammed the Labor government for grounding the vehicles before fire season."It's only literally ... October 3, (that) the Premier was talking about the upcoming fire season, highlighting that it's going to be potentially a difficult fire season," Mr O'Brien said.
  Instance 2: "If that's the case, we need to have every available asset that we can. The government needs to come out today and explain what the implications of that are, how they're dealing with it and how they're going to get those firefighting vehicles back on-stream."FFMVic reportedly brought additional vehicles online for bushfire season preparedness and in the event of an emergency.Mr O'Brien, who is also the opposition spokesperson for emergency services, said he was particularly concerned  the retirement of the fleet would mean a reliance on Country Fire Authority volunteers. A CFA spokesperson said the organisation has been working closely with partners to prepare for the summer."Forest Fire Management Victoria (FFMVic) has been keeping CFA informed of the progress of the current fleet repairs, and we have assisted FFMV with the provision of fire vehicles that were due to go to disposal," the spokesperson said. "CFA will assist FFMV as we always have, in a joint and complementary manner."Mr O'Brien also pointed to the  emergency services and volunteers fund levy, which came into effect on July 1, 2025 ."Victorians are paying an additional $3 billion through Labor's new emergency services tax," he said. "Yet the CFA is relying on ageing vehicles and is now being asked to cover for FFMVic, an organisation now being funded by these additional taxes."A protest against the emergency services levy at Chesney Vale in the North East.

  Instance 1: urn:contentItem:6H04-4073-RS3K-21G8-00000-00Mercedes firefighting trucks taken off road for repair before summer starts2025-10-16T00:00:00Z2025-11-03T19:29:32ZLexisNexisMercedes firefighting trucks taken off road for repair before summer startsChelsea Wilson'Our crown land firefighting fleet has been significantly impacted.'Forest Fire Management Victoria has removed hundreds of Mercedes-Benz firefighting vehicles from service due to safety concerns.After routine inspections revealed issues with the vehicles, 280 G-wagons and 59 Unimogs have been taken off the road to be checked and repaired if necessary."These repairs are being fast-tracked over the next two months," a Victorian government spokesperson said. "FFMVic is working on agreements to secure additional emergency response vehicles from other states if required."The vehicles are used by FFMVic for accessing remote terrain and have been grounded because of cracking issues with the chassis on the G-wagons.Victorian Nationals leader Danny O'Brien slammed the Labor government for grounding the vehicles before fire season."It's only literally last Friday [October 3], the Premier was talking about the upcoming fire season, highlighting that it's going to be potentially a difficult fire season," Mr O'Brien said. "If that's the case, we need to have every available asset that we can."The government needs to come out today and explain what the implications of that are, how they're dealing with it and how they're going to get those firefighting vehicles back on-stream."FFMVic reportedly brought additional vehicles online for bushfire season preparedness and in the event of an emergency.Mr O'Brien, who is also the opposition spokesperson for emergency services, said he was particularly concerned  the retirement of the fleet would mean a reliance on Country Fire Authority volunteers.

  Instance 1: urn:contentItem:6GXR-VGH3-RSJY-54KY-00000-00State's frontline fire fleet crippled2025-10-09T00:00:00Z2025-11-03T19:29:32ZLexisNexisNEWSPg. 3State's frontline fire fleet crippledEXCLUSIVE Shannon DeeryVictoria's forest firefighting capability has been crippled just weeks before the fire season with dozens of response -vehicles pulled off the road due to safety concerns.The Herald Sun can reveal Forest Fire Management Victoria has been forced to ground its entire G-Wagon fleet and multiple heavy tanker Unimog vehicles that have been found with "subframe cracks", raising questions about their roadworthiness.Authorities have been working since Saturday to put back- up plans in place, and have considered calling on extra CFA support, a move that threatens to stretch already overworked brigades.Problems with the vehicles - used by Forest Fire Management Victoria for rapid -responses to outbreaks and to access remote terrain - were identified on -Friday, just one day after Premier Jacinta Allan warned that Victoria was heading -towards a significantly dangerous fire season."The advice we are receiving as a government is that this is one of the most dangerous seasons we are heading into for some time," she said then.The vehicles were rolled out from 2017 as part of a $32m -upgrade of the state's firefighting vehicles.Opposition emergency services spokesman Danny O'Brien said Victorians needed to know what contingencies were in place to protect communities."Labor promised Victorians a state-of-the-art firefighting fleet; eight years later Labor has delivered a world-class failure," Mr O'Brien said. "When the Premier warns of a dangerous fire season, Victorians -deserve answers on how this failure was allowed to -happen and what steps will be taken to ensure community safety."Victorians are paying an additional $3bn through Labor's new emergency services tax, yet the CFA is relying on ageing vehicles and is now being asked to cover for FFMV, an organisation now being funded by these additional taxes." Opposition public land management spokeswoman Melina Bath slammed the government for leaving regional Victoria exposed."Grounding Victoria's frontline fleet weeks before fire season is an unacceptable failure, given nearly 40 per cent of the state is public land," Ms Bath said. "Victorians are paying more but getting less protection." A government spokesman confirmed safety checks had identified issues on almost 300 vehicles, with repairs to be "fast-tracked over the next two months"."The safety of our firefighters is paramount, that's why regular safety inspections of vehicles and equipment are so important," he said."FFMVic has already completed its bushfire preparedness work for the coming season and has the vehicle capacity to respond in a bushfire emergency." The spokesman said a contingency fleet was available as well as Landcruiser vehicles, Fire Tankers and bulldozers.

  Instance 1: urn:contentItem:6H0G-25G3-RRJD-94X6-00000-00Missing man Troy Milne found alive in bushland more than two hours from campsite2025-10-17T00:00:00Z2025-11-03T19:29:32ZLexisNexisMissing man Troy Milne found alive in bushland more than two hours from campsiteBy Madeleine Stuchbery and Zaida Glibanovic A man who was missing in Victoria's east for more than a week is recovering in hospital after being found in bushland when he started a fire to draw attention to his location.A man who went missing for more than a week in Victorian bushland has been found by police, more than two hours away from his campsite.61-year-old Troy Milne, from Cockatoo, was camping with his wife at Woodside Beach in the state's south-east when he went missingwhile picking up supplies on October 7. He was found around 5pm on Thursday evening in Buchan in East Gippsland after an extensive nine-day search operation.Police had concerns for Mr Milne's health, as he is an insulin-dependent diabetic. He was discovered near his Jeep Wrangler close to the Kirby Cross Track after Forest Fire Management Victoria (FFMVic) responded to reports of a fire. Wellington Police Service Area Inspector Wayne Rothwell said he was found dehydrated, but was OK. "His medical condition caused him to become confused," Inspector Rothwell said.
  Instance 2: "It appears Troy has lit a fire to bring attention to himself," Inspector Rothwell said. Mr Milne has been taken to hospital for treatment and observation. Some scientists challenge logic of Victoria's fuel reduction burns [3]
  Instance 1: But some scientists are asking if fuel burns are the best way to reduce fire risk. Planned burns are a cornerstone of Australian bushfire preparedness. And a dry winter in regional Victoria throughout 2025 has presented forest fire management teams with opportunities for extra fuel load reduction burns. But as Victorians brace for heightened fire risks this summer, particularly in western and south-western regions of the state, a growing chorus of ecologists and environmentalists is challenging the planned burns methodology.Some say planned burns are causing more harm than good, with resources better directed to new technologies and a more bespoke approach to fuel reduction ahead of the fire season. Country Fire Authority (CFA) assistant chief fire officer Brian Russell said conditions, particularly in South Gippsland, had been dry during winter and into spring.
  Instance 2: He said while rain was on the way this spring, it was "not going to make a big difference". "The fire danger is still there," Mr Russell said. "As soon as we get a bit of sun and a bit of wind, we will have those fire conditions again."Peter Brick is a regional manager for Forest Fire Management Victoria (FFMVic) in Gippsland. He said autumn and winter presented opportunities to undertake extra fuel reduction in the state. "We were able to treat nearly 40,000 hectares of public lands across 81 different planned burns," he said."They'll provide immediate benefit this summer to reduce the risk of bushfire to the community."Other fuel reduction works conducted throughout winter include fuel break maintenance, roadside slashing, and track maintenance.
  Instance 3: FFMVic chief fire officer Chris Hardman said its bushfire risk management program was underpinned by a significant body of evidence and the department continued to invest in research and the best science. "We use science and modelling tools to choose the right time and approach to deliver our bushfire risk management program, including planned burns, mowing, slashing and spraying," he said. "We know from both research and practical experience that fuel management slows the spread of fire, and helps firefighters reduce threats to communities, critical infrastructure and the environment."ABCPNW-105666680ABCPNW2025urn:contentItem:6H13-94M3-SJ80-B2RS-00000-003002242025-10-20Copyright 2025 Australian Broadcasting Corporation All Rights ReservedABC Premium News (Australia)October 20, 2025 MondayWeb PublicationWeb-based PublicationsENGLISHDisasters, Accidents and Emergency Incidents:Disasters and Hazards:Fires:BushfiresDisasters, Accidents and Emergency Incidents:Disaster and Emergency Response:Emergency ServicesDisasters, Accidents and Emergency Incidents:Disaster and Emergency ResponseGovernment and Politics:State and Territory GovernmentAustralia:VIC:SaleAustralia:VIC:WarragulST000DRETPRESCRIBED FIRESST000DT12TECHNOLOGYST000DTIOFIRE MANAGEMENTST0009SI7ENVIRONMENTALISMSTX001826WEATHERST000D1BYEXECUTIVESST000DSY2DISASTER RISK REDUCTIONST000DT1HNATURAL SCIENCESSTX001949LAND USE &amp; DEVELOPMENTSTX001940ENVIRONMENT &amp; NATURAL RESOURCESSTX001009FOREST FIRESST000DLX0PUBLIC LANDSSTX001964SCIENCE &amp; TECHNOLOGYSTX001066MANAGERS &amp; SUPERVISORSST0009FY2ECOLOGY &amp; ENVIRONMENTAL SCIENCEST000CEC1FIRE PREVENTION &amp; SAFETYST000DOX0WILDFIRESSTX000726FIRESST0009JY5COLLEGE &amp; UNIVERSITY PROFESSORSST000DOQLAUSTRALIAN BUSHFIRESST000DRETPRESCRIBED FIRESST0009JY5COLLEGE &amp; UNIVERSITY PROFESSORSGS007VICTORIA, AUSTRALIAGC301AUSTRALIAEnergy &amp; Utilities LawZ3VpZD11cm46dG9waWM6OUUzODAyRDk1QzVFNEZGMEJDM0RGMDYxOTlEMEEzRDA7cGFyZW50Z3VpZD0General OverviewZ3VpZD11cm46dG9waWM6QUE5QTI3M0EzMzA2NERGRjk0NUM1RjBEMzNBMTJGMTI7cGFyZW50Z3VpZD11cm46dG9waWM6NTY1MkM5NEQwRkY0NDEwNjgwM0JBNUQyNzNFM0QwNkYEnvironmental LawZ3VpZD11cm46dG9waWM6NzFDRDYyNkI2QjhBNDg3NTkyRjRDRkZEQjlCRkRBQzM7cGFyZW50Z3VpZD0Forest ManagementZ3VpZD11cm46dG9waWM6RkRGMjQxNzgzQ0RFNEQ4QkEwQ0U0MUEzOUVBREI3Nzk7cGFyZW50Z3VpZD11cm46dG9waWM6NTkwMDY1RDExQ0YwNDQ1RTlERUVFMjUzMUI1MkFDOTU
