Burn-off fiasco risks LA repeat [2]
  Instance 1: urn:contentItem:6H43-40P3-RRVV-D1TV-00000-00Burn-off fiasco risks LA repeat2025-11-03T00:00:00Z2025-11-03T19:29:32ZLexisNexisTHENATIONPg. 6Burn-off fiasco risks LA repeatJOHN FERGUSON ASSOCIATE EDITORAustralia's most exposed bushfire areas are facing Los Angeles or Black Saturday-style community disasters because of a failure to -accept royal commission -demands on burn-offs.Bushfire experts say Victoria's neglect to come anywhere near burning off targets set by the Black Saturday royal commission has exposed large areas to crippling fires, including heavily populated centres.The Howitt Society has warned that the halving of burn-offs and other mitigation measures under Labor since 2014 has set the scene for potential dis-asters that would rival the impact of this year's Los Angeles fires where more than 17,000 homes, businesses and other buildings were destroyed.While about 30 people died, the fires were dwarfed in human terms by the 2009 Black Saturday fires in Victoria where 173 people died.Howitt Society secretary Garry Squires said Victoria was meant to burn off 5 per cent of public land each year to reduce fuel loads under the royal commission recommendation. The Australian has calculated that number was running at about 1.5 per cent in 2023-24, the estimation based on publicly available information.Mr Squires warned that NSW was also exposed and there was broad risk of another disaster in Victoria: "It just could go wrong." He said this meant the fire risk had soared and that heavily populated areas in Victoria including the Dandenongs, Yarra Valley, Otway Ranges and Mornington Peninsula were at high risk.Asked whether the Victorian government had done enough, he said: "It certainly has not." Fire safety is looming as a potentially major issue at the next Victorian election after Labor overhauled fire fighting services and imposed an unpopular fire services tax.Forest Fire Management Victoria is working in an environment of extreme budget pressure but with a growing population that continues to encroach on rural areas, especially in the interface zones outside Melbourne.The Black Saturday royal commission backed a then doubling of prescribed burn-offs to 5 per cent of public land but Victoria deemed in 2016 that the target was not achievable.Climate variability has also reduced the window of opportunity for burning off in the nearly nine million hectares of public land.Opposition public land spokeswoman Melina Bath said Labor's failure to manage fuel loads had been an act of "reckless -complacency"."Labor's neglect of Victoria's public forests is a disaster waiting to happen; its fuel reduction program has collapsed from around 200,000ha to barely 100,000ha," the Nationals MP said."Labor stopped fuel load mapping in 2020, leaving communities completely in the dark. Regional Victorians live with the consequences of Labor's mismanagement each and every fire season." The hardest hit areas on Black Saturday in 2009 included Marysville on the edge of the Yarra -Ranges, where 34 people died and hundreds of buildings, mainly houses, were wiped out .The fire season in Victoria, South Australian and Tasmania - typically the worst areas in Australia - tends to start later in the season compared with Queensland and NSW.The severity of the season will hinge on full loads, dryness of the fuel, temperature on any day, wind severity and topography.Victoria's Dandenong Ranges and Otway National Forest are well overdue for major fires, potentially affecting thousands of people.Acting FFMVic chief fire officer Scott Turner said emergency services were well-prepared "for all emerging risks" linked to an earlier bushfire season.He said FFMVic used every possible time to cut the risk through planned burns and other so-called mechanical means such as mowing, spraying, fuel breaks and maintaining road access."Reducing bushfire risk occurs throughout the year," he said. "Our long-term strategy focuses on building a strategic network of fuel-reduced areas across public land, not just through one burn or one year, but through ongoing planned action." Risk minimisation also focused on emergency warning systems and community engagement.A core issue in the royal commission report was the lack of proper communications systems, especially around fire locations.
  Instance 2: Regional Victorians live with the consequences of Labor's mismanagement each and every fire season." The hardest hit areas on Black Saturday in 2009 included Marysville on the edge of the Yarra -Ranges, where 34 people died and hundreds of buildings, mainly houses, were wiped out .The fire season in Victoria, South Australian and Tasmania - typically the worst areas in Australia - tends to start later in the season compared with Queensland and NSW.The severity of the season will hinge on full loads, dryness of the fuel, temperature on any day, wind severity and topography.Victoria's Dandenong Ranges and Otway National Forest are well overdue for major fires, potentially affecting thousands of people.Acting FFMVic chief fire officer Scott Turner said emergency services were well-prepared "for all emerging risks" linked to an earlier bushfire season.He said FFMVic used every possible time to cut the risk through planned burns and other so-called mechanical means such as mowing, spraying, fuel breaks and maintaining road access."Reducing bushfire risk occurs throughout the year," he said. "Our long-term strategy focuses on building a strategic network of fuel-reduced areas across public land, not just through one burn or one year, but through ongoing planned action." Risk minimisation also focused on emergency warning systems and community engagement.A core issue in the royal commission report was the lack of proper communications systems, especially around fire locations. Since Black Saturday, an inevitable sense of complacency has hit some areas, especially among so-called tree changers, who have -arrived in areas that are impossible to defend.THEAUS-afe1f0f0b77411f0a4de1b055b24c5b2d50c08f5e21f509cf70a320e9410a5fdTHEAUS2025urn:contentItem:6H43-40P3-RRVV-D1TV-00000-002447772025-11-02Copyright 2025 Nationwide News Pty Limited All Rights ReservedThe AustralianAustralian EditionNovember 3, 2025 MondayNewspaperNewspapersENGLISHST000D1DRNEGATIVE NEWSSTX001511RURAL COMMUNITIESST000DRETPRESCRIBED FIRESST00095ADFOREST RESOURCES MANAGEMENTST000DTIOFIRE MANAGEMENTSTX002021SAFETYSTX001949LAND USE &amp; DEVELOPMENTSTX000453DEATH &amp; DYINGSTX001009FOREST FIRESST000DLX0PUBLIC LANDSSTX001987FORESTS &amp; WOODLANDSSTX001963SAFETY, ACCIDENTS &amp; DISASTERSST0009QD4NEGATIVE BUSINESS NEWSST000CEC1FIRE PREVENTION &amp; SAFETYST000DOX0WILDFIRESSTX000726FIRESST000DRETPRESCRIBED FIRESST00095ADFOREST RESOURCES MANAGEMENTSTX000218BUDGETSGX015MELBOURNE, AUSTRALIAGS007VICTORIA, AUSTRALIAGS001NEW SOUTH WALES, AUSTRALIAGC301AUSTRALIABusiness &amp; Corporate ComplianceZ3VpZD11cm46dG9waWM6MUFEMUQ2QTA1OUZCNEE5RjkzNTA2RERFMUNEOTk1RTI7cGFyZW50Z3VpZD0Overtime &amp; Work PeriodsZ3VpZD11cm46dG9waWM6MDIyRUUyMjlBMjdCNEQ1QkFGMDIyNUIyRDc2QTYzNjI7cGFyZW50Z3VpZD11cm46dG9waWM6RTZBOUIyNzU3RjkxNDQ1QUE3MUZDQjUxOTRENTUzMkQEnvironmental LawZ3VpZD11cm46dG9waWM6NzFDRDYyNkI2QjhBNDg3NTkyRjRDRkZEQjlCRkRBQzM7cGFyZW50Z3VpZD0Forest ManagementZ3VpZD11cm46dG9waWM6RkRGMjQxNzgzQ0RFNEQ4QkEwQ0U0MUEzOUVBREI3Nzk7cGFyZW50Z3VpZD11cm46dG9waWM6NTkwMDY1RDExQ0YwNDQ1RTlERUVFMjUzMUI1MkFDOTULabor &amp; Employment LawZ3VpZD11cm46dG9waWM6MTE3QUQwOTA0MUYzNDlCMEFFMjUwRUNDM0RDRkM5QzM7cGFyZW50Z3VpZD0Overtime &amp; Work PeriodsZ3VpZD11cm46dG9waWM6MDIyRUUyMjlBMjdCNEQ1QkFGMDIyNUIyRDc2QTYzNjI7cGFyZW50Z3VpZD11cm46dG9waWM6RTZBOUIyNzU3RjkxNDQ1QUE3MUZDQjUxOTRENTUzMkQ

  Instance 1: urn:contentItem:6GVP-VXK3-RSRC-H4CY-00000-00Firefighter's warning as off-season grassfire burns out of control2025-09-29T00:00:00Z2025-11-03T19:29:32ZLexisNexisFirefighter's warning as off-season grassfire burns out of controlDocument links may not lead to an active page. Page maintenance is at the discretion of the publisher.Timothy CoxA grassfire burnt out of control near Ballarat on Monday afternoon, prompting an unusually large emergency response for the pre-fire season period.A CFA spokesman said 27 crews and 90 personnel in total were called to tackle the grass and scrubfire that broke out near Berringa about 1.30pm."Crews discovered a large grassfire producing a significant amount of smoke,'' the spokesman said."The grassfire is located in difficult terrain."Air support and Forest Fire Management Victoria were called to the scene to assist.VicEmergency listed a watch and act for residents in Berringa, Cape Clear, Springdallah as the fire moved southeast from Moonlight Creek Rd towards Derwent Jacks and Staffordshire Reef Roads.Strong winds and dangerous trees slowed down firefighers' efforts early on.As of Monday afternoon, about 10ha had been burnt on the private parcel of land.The fire was deemed under control at 6.24pm and safe at 8.18pm.CFA incident controller and Grenville Group officer Greg Parker said investigations continued regarding the cause of the fire."Obviously at the moment there's a lot of people that are burning off in the area trying to clean up before the fire danger period and fire season takes effect, so people just need to be mindful and make sure that they black out their fires prior to leaving, especially if it is a weekender that lives elsewhere," he said."The number of appliances and the area that it's burnt is very unusual for this time of year, being so early."But the bush and areas are still quite dry because of the lack of rainfall across the area."CFA members have already begun preparations for the fire When camping trips turn costly: warnings issued as campers ignore fire ban [2]
  Instance 1: urn:contentItem:6GXV-8TB3-RS93-M4YH-00000-00When camping trips turn costly: warnings issued as campers ignore fire ban2025-10-10T00:00:00Z2025-11-03T19:29:32ZLexisNexisWhen camping trips turn costly: warnings issued as campers ignore fire banAmy Rees'Over the long weekend, I personally put out four fires'.IGNORANCE is not an excuse when it comes to lighting campfires during fire ban periods, with the results costly and potentially deadly.Over the October long weekend, Forestry Corporation ranger Paul Robb put out four campfires that were burning, despite a solid fuel fire ban coming into effect on October 1.Mr Robb said he came across fires in Sunny Corner, Vulcan, Jenolan, and Lisdale State Forests.This is Mr Robb's third October long weekend patrolling the region's state forests, and each year he has come across people lighting campfires."It happens every year ... it is very frustrating," he said."Over the long weekend, I personally put out four fires that were burning."People just claimed they weren't aware."Mr Robb said ignorance won't save people from having to pay the $550 on-the-spot fine, which is given to everyone sitting around and using the fire, not just the person who lit it.In addition to the fine, people are also liable for any damage their campfire causes if it becomes out of control.And with plantations worth approximately $140,000 per hectare, a simple weekend away could end up costly.But the biggest cost of all is the safety of forest users.Mr Robb said an out-of-control forest fire becomes very dangerous very quickly, to everyone in the forest at the time."People don't realise the danger they put themselves and other forest users in, let alone the damage to our business," he said."We're responsible for all forest users, but we're also responsible to the business."It's a taxpayer business of pine plantation. So we're responsible for looking after that asset for the taxpayer, and if it gets burnt, that's not a good thing."From October 1 until April 30 - subject to fire conditions - no solid fuel, wood fires or little ovens are permitted in state forests.Mr Paul said campers can only use gas appliances, and even then, cannot leave them unattended at any time.He asks that people enjoying the forests for their recreational activities simply follow the regulations, for the safety of themselves, others and the plantation.Forestry Corporation ranger Paul Robb reminds forest users the fire ban has commenced. Picture suppliedForestry Corporation ranger Paul Robb reminds forest users the fire ban has commenced.
  Instance 2: So we're responsible for looking after that asset for the taxpayer, and if it gets burnt, that's not a good thing."From October 1 until April 30 - subject to fire conditions - no solid fuel, wood fires or little ovens are permitted in state forests.Mr Paul said campers can only use gas appliances, and even then, cannot leave them unattended at any time.He asks that people enjoying the forests for their recreational activities simply follow the regulations, for the safety of themselves, others and the plantation.Forestry Corporation ranger Paul Robb reminds forest users the fire ban has commenced. Cause of fire at Berringa under investigation after evacuation warning [2]
  Instance 1: urn:contentItem:6GVX-JFF3-RRR6-F0KR-00000-00Cause of fire at Berringa under investigation after evacuation warning2025-10-01T00:00:00Z2025-11-03T19:29:33ZLexisNexisCause of fire at Berringa under investigation after evacuation warningAdam SpencerIt was the first major blaze ahead of the fire season.Fire investigations are looking for the cause of a grass and scrub fire at Berringa, south of Ballarat, after an evacuation warning was issued to residents on Monday afternoon.The fire, on Derwent Jacks Road, ignited just after 1pm on September 29, with 30 CFA units called to the scene about 1.16pm.A CFA spokesperson said the fire was in difficult terrain, spanned across 10 acres and was producing a significant amount of smoke."Forest Fire Management Victoria were called to the scene to assist," the spokesperson said." A Watch and Act, and Advice warning  was issued to the community to stay near shelter and stay Informed."A fire investigator has been called to the scene and investigations are still underway."The CFA said no assets were under threat and the scene was deemed under control at 6.24pm.It was the first major blaze of the season, coming just weeks after the  CFA urged residents in bushfire-prone areas  to get a bushfire plan in place and start preparing their properties for the summer.It also comes as the hay season begins in the western part of Victoria, with farmers being urged to take extra care to prevent haystack fires.Haystack fires are often caused by spontaneous combustion when hay is baled with excess moisture.High moisture levels, combined with the compact nature of hay bales, can create internal heat, leading to ignition.In the 2024/25 financial year, the CFA said it responded to 73 haystack and hay shed fires in regional areas, with 53 per cent occurring in the west and northwest of the state.A CFA truck near the scene of a grass and scrub fire in Berringa, south-west of Ballarat on September 29, 2025. A Watch and Act, and Advice warning  was issued to the community to stay near shelter and stay Informed."A fire investigator has been called to the scene and investigations are still underway."The CFA said no assets were under threat and the scene was deemed under control at 6.24pm.It was the first major blaze of the season, coming just weeks after the  CFA urged residents in bushfire-prone areas  to get a bushfire plan in place and start preparing their properties for the summer.It also comes as the hay season begins in the western part of Victoria, with farmers being urged to take extra care to prevent haystack fires.Haystack fires are often caused by spontaneous combustion when hay is baled with excess moisture.High moisture levels, combined with the compact nature of hay bales, can create internal heat, leading to ignition.In the 2024/25 financial year, the CFA said it responded to 73 haystack and hay shed fires in regional areas, with 53 per cent occurring in the west and northwest of the state.A CFA truck near the scene of a grass and scrub fire in Berringa, south-west of Ballarat on September 29, 2025. BREAKING BARRIERS [2]
  Instance 1: 7BREAKING BARRIERSTESSA HAYWARDTYSON NEAL-EDWARDS IS RUNNING IN THE NEW YORK CITY MARATHON TOMORROW, BUT HE TELLS TESSA HAYWARD THE REAL JOURNEY STARTS WHEN HE FINISHES IT The sound of his feet hitting the pavement is all that Tyson Neal-Edwards hears when he is running.There's no music blaring through headphones or any distractions. Instead, this is his time to think.Six months ago, the 23-year-old had never even considered running a marathon, let alone going on runs consistently.But his decision to apply for the Indigenous Marathon Project (IMP) Squad, and be selected first go, changed everything.The proud Gunditjmara, Wadawurrung and Arrernte man will take on the New York City Marathon tomorrow as part of the IMP Squad of inspiring First Nations runners and changemakers who are breaking barriers, building leadership and creating healthier futures through running.But as Tyson explains, being a part of the IMP Squad is so much more than just running a marathon."It is a leadership and development program at its core," he says. To apply for the six-month program, applicants must not have run a marathon before and be aged between 18 and30.Twelve Aboriginal and/or Torres Strait Islander people are then selected to train for the New York City Marathon.Education is a compulsory part of the program, which is run by the Indigenous Marathon Foundation, and includes education on leadership, first aid, mental health and media training.Physical and mental boundaries are pushed to a new level and the marathon is used to support members to realise that they can achieve anything.Tyson, who works in forest fire management, says he initially applied as he liked networking with mob and like-minded people."Being in the program has changed my why significantly, it has been a very emotional journey," he shares."I am the oldest of seven siblings and I want to lead by action. Action speaks louder than words so I want to do my best and show them that."You can be what you can't see, they don't have to run marathons, but you can do anything." Training for the marathon started six months ago and Tyson says they started with the Mother's Day Classic 10km in Canberra in May, followed by half marathons on the Gold Coast and Sunshine Coast.The 30km election run in Alice Springs was their final challenge, It was the most emotional for Tyson, with both his nan and sister there supporting him.If all these runs are completed, you are selected to go to New York. "It's been pretty hard, challenging in a few aspects, not just physically but mentally.
  Instance 2: "I thoroughly enjoy that part of the day when I have no distractions, no phone," he says."I get to calm down and think about things I didn't want to think about and I love hearing my feet. You get in a flow state," he says."I'm so happy I can share my story, particularly for my mum and my nan. They made me who I am today." ON THE BACKBURNER [2]
  Instance 1: urn:contentItem:6H31-8523-RSR8-53TT-00000-00ON THE BACKBURNER2025-10-29T00:00:00Z2025-11-03T19:29:32ZLexisNexisNEWSPg. 1ON THE BACKBURNERPETER HUNT and DAVID JOHNSTONYears of neglect have left Victorians at risk, in what is shaping up to be one of the worst fire seasons in more than a decade.A lack of resources has meant a steady decline in fuel reduction burns, which state government records show have slumped from about 200,000ha annually, when Labor came to power in late 2014, to about 100,000ha in recent years.That decline comes despite the Allan government raking in an extra $540m in fire services tax this financial year.Howitt Society president Peter Flinn said fuel reduction burns now amounted to little more than 1 per cent of Victoria's public land each year, "just one fifth of the minimum recommended per annum by the royal commission into the horrendous 2009 Black Saturday fires, which claimed 173 lives"."We are frequently told by FFMV (Forest Fire Management Victoria) they would like to do more in terms of fuel management, but are constrained by a shortage of funds and/or manpower, objections from some sections of the community, and that climate change is 'narrowing the windows' for suitable weather conditions," he said. The government has admitted FFMV funding has fallen from $441.3m 2024-25 to $400.6m this financial year, but stated it was the result of specific project funding for emergency management reforms coming to an end.However Mr Flinn said the lack of resources meant fuel reduction burns that FFMVic promised to undertake in the Southern Grampians this spring had not occurred, as thousands of tonnes of fuel built up in the canopy and the forest floor.Further east FFMVic has cleared windblown trees from 1100ha of the 44,700ha Wombat-Lerderderg Forest, but has admitted there are large areas where thousands of logs remain lying on the forest floor from 2021 storms.Bush User Groups United representative Stephen Smitham said the situation could get a lot worse, once the government locked up 75,000ha of the forest in new parks and reserves, under legislation before Parliament's Upper House this week. "I'd already be worried about going into the forest if I was a CFA volunteer," Mr Smitham said.
  Instance 2: If it gets into that regrowth from the 2019-20 fires on the road between Ensay and Bruthen it would go off like a nuclear bomb." As FFMVic struggles to reduce fuel loads the Allan government has almost doubled fire service taxes on Victorian households and businesses, from $839m in 2023-24 to $1.54bn this financial year, with another hike to $1.8bn in 2026-27.Premier Jacinta Allan and her Treasurer Jaclyn Symes have repeatedly stated "every dollar" of the emergency services volunteer tax would be used to fund emergency services, but have repeatedly refused to detail how much extra is going to FFMVic and the CFA in 2025-26.When asked to provide details of the CFA's 2025-26 budget, Treasurer Symes office simply stated details would be released in the agency's annual report, which is unlikely to be released until after next year's November 28 state election.Meanwhile, Victorians have been left in the dark on just how much fuel has built up in forests that cover a third of the state. In 2020 the government stopped publishing fuel load maps for fear they could be used by arsonists, an argument the nation's leading bushfire scientists branded "ludicrous" and "a load of rubbish".Since then the government has simply reported on statewide and regional fuel-driven bushfire risk reduction targets.The government has set at a statewide target that equates to reducing the loss of life and property to 70 per cent of what would have occurred if no planned burning or major fires had occurred (100 per cent).But even then access to the latest 2024-25 risk report has been delayed until December.The most recent publicly available report for 2023-24 showed the bushfire risk at a regional level had reached 92 per cent in Melbourne's foothills, the Dandenongs and Mornington Peninsula, worse than in the lead-up to the 2009 Black Saturday fires.When asked to supply the 2024-25 risk reports FFMVic stated they would not be released until December.
